data-file-height="1110" data-file-width="1105" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/2004_FL_Proof.png/85px-2004_FL_Proof.png" style="text-align:center;border-top:#aaa 1px solid"><a href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_symbols" title="Lists of United States state symbols">Lists of United States state symbols</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Florida</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">f</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/\xc9\x92r/: \'or\' in \'moral\'">\xc9\x92r</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\xc9\x99</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Florida.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a>\xc2\xa0</span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/36/En-us-Florida.ogg" title="En-us-Florida.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> (Spanish for "land of flowers") is the southernmost <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">southeastern region</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The state is bordered to the west by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, to the north by Alabama and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, and to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a>. Florida is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">22nd-most extensive</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">3rd-most populous</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014pop_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014pop-9">[9]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">8th-most densely populated</a> of the U.S. states. <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Florida" title="List of municipalities in Florida">most populous municipality</a> in the state and the largest city by area in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a> (due to the consolidation of Jacksonville with <a href="/wiki/Duval_County,_Florida" title="Duval County, Florida">Duval County</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami metropolitan area</a> is Florida\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_urbanized_areas_in_Florida_(by_population)" title="List of urbanized areas in Florida (by population)">most populous urban area</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tallahassee,_Florida" title="Tallahassee, Florida">Tallahassee</a> is the state\'s capital.</p>\n<p>About two-thirds of Florida occupies a peninsula between the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. Florida has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_coastline" title="List of U.S. states by coastline">longest coastline</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>, approximately 1,350 miles (2,170\xc2\xa0km), not including the contribution of the many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrier_Island" title="Barrier Island">barrier islands</a>. It is the only state that borders both the Gulf of Mexico and the Atlantic Ocean. Much of the state is at or near sea level and is characterized by <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sedimentary</a> soil. Florida has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_elevation" title="List of U.S. states by elevation">lowest high point</a> of any U.S. state. The climate varies from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> in the north to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">tropical</a> in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abbott_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-abbott-10">[10]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_alligator" title="American alligator">American alligator</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_crocodile" title="American crocodile">American crocodile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_panther" title="Florida panther">Florida panther</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">manatee</a> can be found in <a href="/wiki/Everglades_National_Park" title="Everglades National Park">Everglades National Park</a> in the southern part of the state. Florida is one of only two states that has a tropical climate, the other one is <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> and is the only continental U.S. State with a tropical climate.</p>\n<p>Since the first European contact was made in 1513 by Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 who named it <i>La Florida</i> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[la flo\xcb\x88\xc9\xbei\xc3\xb0a]</a></span> "land of flowers") upon landing there in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easter_season" title="Easter season">Easter season</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pascua_Florida" title="Pascua Florida">Pascua Florida</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 Florida was a challenge for the European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial powers</a> before it gained statehood in the United States in 1845. It was a principal location of the <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars" title="Seminole Wars">Seminole Wars</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>, and racial segregation after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>.</p>\n<p>Today, Florida is distinctive for its large <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuban</a> expatriate community and high population growth, as well as for its increasing environmental issues. The state\'s economy relies mainly on tourism, agriculture, and <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Florida" title="Transportation in Florida">transportation</a>, which developed in the late 19th century. Florida is also renowned for <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement parks</a>, orange crops, the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a>, and as a popular destination for retirees.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Florida" title="Culture of Florida">Florida culture</a> is a reflection of influences and multiple inheritance; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_American" title="European American">European</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a> heritages can be found in the architecture and cuisine. Florida has attracted many writers such as <a href="/wiki/Marjorie_Kinnan_Rawlings" title="Marjorie Kinnan Rawlings">Marjorie Kinnan Rawlings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Williams" title="Tennessee Williams">Tennessee Williams</a>, and continues to attract celebrities and athletes. It is internationally known for golf, tennis, auto racing and <a href="/wiki/List_of_water_sports" title="List of water sports">water sports</a>.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Intercity_rail"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Intercity rail</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Public_transit"><span class="tocnumber">10.4</span> <span class="toctext">Public transit</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Sister_states"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sister states</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Florida" title="History of Florida">History of Florida</a></div>\n<p>By the 16th century (the earliest time for which there is a historical record), major <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> groups included the <a href="/wiki/Apalachee" title="Apalachee">Apalachee</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">Florida Panhandle</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Timucua" title="Timucua">Timucua</a> (of northern and central Florida), the <a href="/wiki/Ais_people" title="Ais people">Ais</a> (of the central Atlantic coast), the <a href="/wiki/Tocobaga" title="Tocobaga">Tocobaga</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay" title="Tampa Bay">Tampa Bay</a> area), the <a href="/wiki/Calusa" title="Calusa">Calusa</a> (of southwest Florida) and the <a href="/wiki/Tequesta" title="Tequesta">Tequesta</a> (of the southeastern coast).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival">European arrival</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1868" data-file-width="2748" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg/200px-Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg/300px-Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg/400px-Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chiaves-la-florida-1584.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap of Florida, likely based on the expeditions of Hernando de Soto (1539\xe2\x80\x931543).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2059" data-file-width="13981" height="52" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg/350px-St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg/525px-St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg/700px-St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._Augustine_Florida_Panoramic_View.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> is one of oldest cities in Florida, established in 1565. The Spanish-Floridan color scheme of red and white is repeated throughout downtown.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1748" data-file-width="5487" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg/350px-Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg/525px-Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg/700px-Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_San_Marcos_Fort_Panorama_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Castillo_de_San_Marcos" title="Castillo de San Marcos">Castillo de San Marcos</a>. Originally white with red corners, its design reflects the colors and shapes of the <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Burgundy" title="Cross of Burgundy">Cross of Burgundy</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Florida" title="Flag of Florida">Flag of Florida</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey,_Galvez_en_America.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1871" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg/200px-Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg/300px-Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg/400px-Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey%2C_Galvez_en_America.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuadro_por_espa%C3%B1a_y_por_el_rey,_Galvez_en_America.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGrenadiers led by <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez">Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pensacola" title="Siege of Pensacola">Siege of Pensacola</a>. Painting by <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Ferrer-Dalmau" title="Augusto Ferrer-Dalmau">Augusto Ferrer-Dalmau</a>, 2015.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Florida was the first region of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" title="Continental United States">continental United States</a> to be visited and settled by Europeans. The earliest known European explorers came with the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>. Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n spotted and landed on the peninsula on April 2, 1513. He named the region <i>La Florida</i> ("land of flowers").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Names_on_the_Land:_A_Historical_Account_of_Place-Naming_in_the_United_States_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Names_on_the_Land:_A_Historical_Account_of_Place-Naming_in_the_United_States-12">[12]</a></sup> The story that he was searching for the <a href="/wiki/Fountain_of_Youth" title="Fountain of Youth">Fountain of Youth</a> is mythical and only appeared long after his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In May 1539, Conquistador <a href="/wiki/Hernando_de_Soto" title="Hernando de Soto">Hernando de Soto</a> skirted the coast of Florida, searching for a deep harbor to land. He described seeing a thick wall of red mangroves spread mile after mile, some reaching as high as 70 feet (21\xc2\xa0m), with intertwined and elevated roots making landing difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The Spanish introduced Christianity, cattle, horses, sheep, the Castilian language, and more to Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A more detailed citation is required. (July 2013)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Spain established several settlements in Florida, with varying degrees of success. In 1559, Don <a href="/wiki/Trist%C3%A1n_de_Luna_y_Arellano" title="Trist\xc3\xa1n de Luna y Arellano">Trist\xc3\xa1n de Luna y Arellano</a> established a settlement at present-day <a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">Pensacola</a>, making it the first attempted settlement in Florida, but it was mostly abandoned by 1561.</p>\n<p>In 1565, the settlement of <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> (San Agust\xc3\xadn) was established under the leadership of admiral and governor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Men%C3%A9ndez_de_Avil%C3%A9s" title="Pedro Men\xc3\xa9ndez de Avil\xc3\xa9s">Pedro Men\xc3\xa9ndez de Avil\xc3\xa9s</a>, creating what would become the oldest European settlement in the continental U.S. and establishing the first generation of Floridanos and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_governors_of_Florida" title="List of colonial governors of Florida">government of Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Spain maintained tenuous control over the region by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_Florida" title="Spanish missions in Florida">converting the local tribes</a> to Christianity.</p>\n<p>The geographical area of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a> diminished with the establishment of English settlements to the north and French claims to the west. The English attacked St. Augustine, burning the city and its cathedral to the ground several times. Spain built the <a href="/wiki/Castillo_de_San_Marcos" title="Castillo de San Marcos">Castillo de San Marcos</a> in 1672 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Matanzas" title="Fort Matanzas">Fort Matanzas</a> in 1742 to defend Florida\'s capital city from attacks, and to maintain its strategic position in the defense of the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Cuba" title="Captaincy General of Cuba">Captaincy General of Cuba</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a>.</p>\n<p>Florida attracted numerous Africans and African-Americans from adjacent British colonies who sought freedom from slavery. In 1738, Governor <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Montiano" title="Manuel de Montiano">Manuel de Montiano</a> established <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mose_Historic_State_Park" title="Fort Mose Historic State Park">Fort Gracia Real de Santa Teresa de Mose</a> near St. Augustine, a fortified town for escaped slaves to whom Montiano granted citizenship and freedom in return for their service in the Florida militia, and which became the first free black settlement legally sanctioned in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-precursor_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-precursor-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Florida_History" title="Timeline of Florida History">1763</a>, Spain traded Florida to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> for control of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, Cuba, which <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Havana_(1762)" title="Battle of Havana (1762)">had been captured</a> by the British during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years\' War">Seven Years\' War</a>. It was part of a large expansion of British territory following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Britain_in_the_Seven_Years_War" title="Great Britain in the Seven Years War">their victory in the Seven Years\' War</a>. A large portion of the Floridano population left, taking along most of the remaining indigenous population to Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http:.2F.2Ffcit.usf.edu.2FFlorida.2Fdocs.2Ff.2Fflorbrit.htm_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-http:.2F.2Ffcit.usf.edu.2FFlorida.2Fdocs.2Ff.2Fflorbrit.htm-19">[19]</a></sup> The British soon constructed the King\'s Road connecting St. Augustine to <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Georgia" title="Province of Georgia">Georgia</a>. The road crossed the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a> at a narrow point, which the <a href="/wiki/Seminole" title="Seminole">Seminole</a> called <i>Wacca Pilatka</i> and the British named "Cow Ford", both names ostensibly reflecting the fact that cattle were brought across the river there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The British divided and consolidated the Florida provinces (<i>Las Floridas</i>) into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_East_Florida" title="British East Florida">East Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_West_Florida" title="British West Florida">West Florida</a>, a division the Spanish government kept after the brief British period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The British government gave land grants to officers and soldiers who had fought in the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> in order to encourage settlement. In order to induce settlers to move to Florida, reports of its natural wealth were published in England. A large number of British settlers who were described as being "energetic and of good character" moved to Florida, mostly coming from <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and England. There was also a group of settlers who came from the colony of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. This would be the first permanent English-speaking population in what is now <a href="/wiki/Duval_County,_Florida" title="Duval County, Florida">Duval County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baker_County,_Florida" title="Baker County, Florida">Baker County</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_County,_Florida" title="St. Johns County, Florida">St. Johns County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_Florida" title="Nassau County, Florida">Nassau County</a>. The British built good public roads and introduced the cultivation of sugar cane, indigo and fruits as well the export of lumber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-25">[25]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As a result of these initiatives northeastern Florida prospered economically in a way it never did under Spanish administration. Furthermore, the British governors were directed to call general assemblies as soon as possible in order to make laws for the Floridas and in the meantime they were, with the advice of councils, to establish courts. This would be the first introduction of much of the English-derived legal system which Florida still has today including <a href="/wiki/Jury_trial" title="Jury trial">trial by jury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habeas_corpus" title="Habeas corpus">habeas corpus</a> and county-based government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-25">[25]</a></sup> Neither East Florida nor West Florida would send any representatives to Philadelphia to draft the Declaration of Independence. Florida would remain a Loyalist stronghold for the duration of the American Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Spain regained both East and West Florida after Britain\'s defeat in the American Revolution and the subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles_(1783)" title="Treaty of Versailles (1783)">Treaty of Versailles</a> in 1783, and continued the provincial divisions until 1821.</p>\n<h3><span id="Joining_the_United_States;_Indian_removal"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Joining_the_United_States.3B_Indian_removal">Joining the United States; Indian removal</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_East_Florida" title="Republic of East Florida">Republic of East Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_Territory" title="Florida Territory">Florida Territory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars" title="Seminole Wars">Seminole Wars</a></div>\n<p>Defense of Florida\'s northern border with the United States was minor during the second Spanish period. The region became a haven for escaped slaves and a base for Indian attacks against U.S. territories, and the U.S. pressed Spain for reform.</p>\n<p>Americans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-American" title="English-American">English descent</a> and Americans of <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_Americans" title="Scotch-Irish Americans">Scots-Irish descent</a> began moving into northern Florida from the backwoods of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>. Though technically not allowed by the Spanish authorities and the Floridan government, they were never able to effectively police the border region and the backwoods settlers from the United States would continue to immigrate into Florida unchecked. These migrants, mixing with the already present British settlers who had remained in Florida since the British period, would be the progenitors of the population known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Cracker" title="Florida Cracker">Florida Crackers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>These American settlers established a permanent foothold in the area and ignored Spanish authorities. The British settlers who had remained also resented Spanish rule, leading to a rebellion in 1810 and the establishment for ninety days of the so-called Free and Independent Republic of <a href="/wiki/West_Florida" title="West Florida">West Florida</a> on September 23. After meetings beginning in June, rebels overcame the garrison at <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">Baton Rouge</a> (now in <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>), and unfurled the flag of the new republic: a single white star on a blue field. This flag would later become known as the "<a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Blue_Flag" title="Bonnie Blue Flag">Bonnie Blue Flag</a>".</p>\n<p>In 1810, parts of West Florida were annexed by proclamation of President <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, who claimed the region as part of the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>. These parts were incorporated into the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Orleans" title="Territory of Orleans">Territory of Orleans</a>. The U.S. annexed the Mobile District of West Florida to the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Territory" title="Mississippi Territory">Mississippi Territory</a> in 1812. Spain continued to dispute the area, though the United States gradually increased the area it occupied. In 1812, a group of settlers from Georgia, with de facto support from the U.S. federal government, attempted to overthrow the Floridan government in the province of East Florida. The settlers hoped to convince Floridans to join their cause and proclaim independence from Spain, but the settlers lost their tenuous support from the federal government and abandoned their cause by 1813.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Seminole" title="Seminole">Seminoles</a> based in <a href="/wiki/East_Florida" title="East Florida">East Florida</a> began raiding Georgia settlements, and offering havens for runaway slaves. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> led increasingly frequent incursions into Spanish territory, including the 1817\xe2\x80\x931818 campaign against the Seminole Indians by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> that became known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Seminole_War" title="First Seminole War">First Seminole War</a>. The United States now effectively controlled East Florida. Control was necessary according to Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a> because Florida had become "a derelict open to the occupancy of every enemy, civilized or savage, of the United States, and serving no other earthly purpose than as a post of annoyance to them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Florida had become a burden to Spain, which could not afford to send settlers or garrisons. Madrid therefore decided to cede the territory to the United States through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adams-On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams-On\xc3\xads Treaty">Adams-On\xc3\xads Treaty</a>, which took effect in 1821.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> was authorized on March 3, 1821 to take possession of <a href="/wiki/East_Florida" title="East Florida">East Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Florida" title="West Florida">West Florida</a> for the United States and provide for initial governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a>, on behalf of the U.S. federal government, served as a military commissioner with the powers of governor of the newly acquired territory for a brief period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On March 30, 1822, the U.S. Congress merged <a href="/wiki/East_Florida" title="East Florida">East Florida</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/West_Florida" title="West Florida">West Florida</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Territory" title="Florida Territory">Florida Territory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="1170" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png/200px-William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png/300px-William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png/400px-William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:William_Cooley_Attack%2BCleaned.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA contemporaneous depiction of the <a href="/wiki/William_Cooley#New_River_Massacre" title="William Cooley">New River Massacre</a> in 1836.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>By the early 1800s, <a href="/wiki/Indian_removal" title="Indian removal">Indian removal</a> was a significant issue throughout the southeastern U.S. and also in Florida. In 1830, the U.S. Congress passed the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Removal_Act" title="Indian Removal Act">Indian Removal Act</a> and as settlement increased, pressure grew on the United States government to remove the Indians from Florida. Seminoles harbored runaway blacks, known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Seminoles" title="Black Seminoles">Black Seminoles</a>, and clashes between whites and Indians grew with the influx of new settlers. In 1832, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Payne%27s_Landing" title="Treaty of Payne\'s Landing">Treaty of Payne\'s Landing</a> promised to the Seminoles lands west of the Mississippi River if they agreed to leave Florida. Many Seminole left at this time.</p>\n<p>Some Seminoles remained, and the U.S. Army arrived in Florida, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Seminole_War" title="Second Seminole War">Second Seminole War</a> (1835\xe2\x80\x931842). Following the war, approximately 3,000 Seminole and 800 Black Seminole were removed to <a href="/wiki/Indian_Territory" title="Indian Territory">Indian Territory</a>. A few hundred Seminole remained in Florida in the <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">Everglades</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="767" data-file-width="600" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg/150px-Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg/225px-Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg/300px-Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Remington_A_cracker_cowboy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA <a href="/wiki/Florida_cracker" title="Florida cracker">Cracker</a> cowboy, 19th century.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On March 3, 1845, Florida became the 27th state to join the United States of America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The state was admitted as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_state" title="Slave state">slave state</a> and ceased to be a sanctuary for runaway slaves. Initially its population grew slowly.</p>\n<p>As European settlers continued to encroach on Seminole lands, and the United States intervened to move the remaining Seminoles to the West. The <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars#Third_Seminole_War" title="Seminole Wars">Third Seminole War</a> (1855\xe2\x80\x9358) resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Trail_of_Tears" title="Trail of Tears">forced removal</a> of most of the remaining Seminoles, although hundreds of Seminole Indians remained in the Everglades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Slavery,_war,_and_disenfranchisement"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery.2C_war.2C_and_disenfranchisement">Slavery, war, and disenfranchisement</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Florida_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Florida in the American Civil War">Florida in the American Civil War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Olustee.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="596" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Battle_of_Olustee.jpg/200px-Battle_of_Olustee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Battle_of_Olustee.jpg/300px-Battle_of_Olustee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Battle_of_Olustee.jpg/400px-Battle_of_Olustee.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Olustee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Olustee" title="Battle of Olustee">Battle of Olustee</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, 1864.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>American settlers began to establish cotton <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">plantations</a> in north Florida, which required numerous laborers, which they supplied by buying slaves in the domestic market. By 1860, Florida had only 140,424 people, of whom 44% were enslaved. There were fewer than 1,000 free <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_black" title="Free black">African Americans</a> before the American Civil War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In January 1861, nearly all delegates in the Florida Legislature approved an ordinance of secession, declaring Florida to be "a sovereign and independent nation"\xe2\x80\x94an apparent reassertion to the preamble in Florida\'s Constitution of 1838, in which Florida agreed with Congress to be a "Free and Independent State." Although not directly related to the issue of slavery, the ordinance declared Florida\'s secession from the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a>, allowing it to become one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States</a>, a looser union of states.</p>\n<p>The confederal union received little help from Florida; the 15,000 men it offered were generally sent elsewhere. The largest engagements in the state were the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Olustee" title="Battle of Olustee">Battle of Olustee</a>, on February 20, 1864, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Natural_Bridge" title="Battle of Natural Bridge">Battle of Natural Bridge</a>, on March 6, 1865. Both were Confederate victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The war ended in 1865.</p>\n<p>Following the American Civil War, Florida\'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">congressional</a> representation was restored on June 25, 1868, albeit forcefully after <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era#Radical_Reconstruction" title="Reconstruction Era">Radical Reconstruction</a> and the installation of unelected government officials under the final authority of federal military commanders. After the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">Reconstruction</a> period ended in 1876, white Democrats regained power in the state legislature. In 1885 they created a new constitution, followed by statutes through 1889 that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">disfranchised</a> most blacks and many poor whites.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>Until the mid-20th century, Florida was the least populous Southern state. In 1900, its population was only 528,542, of whom nearly 44% were African American, the same proportion as before the Civil War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boll_weevil" title="Boll weevil">boll weevil</a> devastated cotton crops.</p>\n<p>Forty thousand blacks, roughly one-fifth of their 1900 population, left the state in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>. They left due to lynchings and racial violence, and for better opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Disfranchisement for most African Americans in the state persisted until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a> of the 1960s gained federal legislation in 1965 to enforce protection of their constitutional suffrage.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th-century_growth">20th-century growth</span></h3>\n<p>Historically, Florida\'s economy has been based primarily upon agricultural products such as cattle, sugar cane, citrus fruits, tomatoes, and strawberries.</p>\n<p>Economic prosperity in the 1920s stimulated tourism to Florida and related development of hotels and resort communities. Combined with its sudden elevation in profile was the <a href="/wiki/Florida_land_boom_of_the_1920s" title="Florida land boom of the 1920s">Florida land boom of the 1920s</a>, which brought a brief period of intense land development. Devastating hurricanes in <a href="/wiki/1926_Miami_hurricane" title="1926 Miami hurricane">1926</a> and <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, brought that period to a halt. Florida\'s economy did not fully recover until the military buildup for <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</p>\n<p>In 1939, Florida was described as \xe2\x80\x9cstill very largely an empty State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Subsequently, the growing availability of <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>, the climate, and a low cost of living made the state a haven. Migration from the <a href="/wiki/Rust_Belt" title="Rust Belt">Rust Belt</a> and the Northeast sharply increased Florida\'s population after 1945. In recent decades, more migrants have come for the jobs in a developing economy.</p>\n<p>With a population of more than 18 million according to the 2010 census, Florida is the most populous state in the southeastern United States and the fourth-most populous in the United States.</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n<div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n<div style="margin:35px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemingwayhouse.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1360" data-file-width="2048" D.C.">D.C.</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n<div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n<div style="margin:30px auto;"><a //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/YborCityAug20087thAvBerniniBricks.jpg/240px-YborCityAug20087thAvBerniniBricks.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Historic <a href="/wiki/Ybor_City" title="Ybor City">Ybor City</a> in Tampa</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n<div style="width: <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami_Historic_District" title="Downtown Miami Historic District">Downtown Miami Historic District</a> has some of the oldest buildings in Miami</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florida_topographic_map-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2810" data-file-width="2890" height="428" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Florida_topographic_map-en.svg/440px-Florida_topographic_map-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Florida_topographic_map-en.svg/660px-Florida_topographic_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Florida_topographic_map-en.svg/880px-Florida_topographic_map-en.svg.png 2x" width="440"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florida_topographic_map-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA topographic map of Florida.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FL_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1231" data-file-width="1080" height="342" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FL_koppen.svg/300px-FL_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FL_koppen.svg/450px-FL_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/FL_koppen.svg/600px-FL_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FL_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nK\xc3\xb6ppen climate types of Florida</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Florida" title="Geography of Florida">Geography of Florida</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Florida" title="List of counties in Florida">List of counties in Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Florida_state_parks" title="List of Florida state parks">List of Florida state parks</a></div>\n<p>Much of the state of Florida is situated on a peninsula between the Gulf of Mexico, the Atlantic Ocean and the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a>. Spanning two <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a>, it extends to the northwest into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhandle" title="Panhandle">panhandle</a>, extending along the northern Gulf of Mexico. It is bordered on the north by the states of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, and on the west, at the end of the panhandle, by Alabama. It is the only state that borders both the Atlantic Ocean and the Gulf of Mexico.</p>\n<p>Florida is west of <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> and 90 miles (140\xc2\xa0km) north of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. Florida is one of the largest states east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>, and only <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> are larger in water area. The water boundary is 3 nautical miles (3.5\xc2\xa0mi; 5.6\xc2\xa0km) offshore in the Atlantic Ocean<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-41">[41]</a></sup> and 9 nautical miles (10\xc2\xa0mi; 17\xc2\xa0km) offshore in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuba-Florida_map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="490" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cuba-Florida_map.jpg/300px-Cuba-Florida_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cuba-Florida_map.jpg/450px-Cuba-Florida_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Cuba-Florida_map.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuba-Florida_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFlorida and its relation to <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>At 345 feet (105\xc2\xa0m) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above mean sea level</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britton_Hill" title="Britton Hill">Britton Hill</a> is the highest point in Florida and the lowest highpoint of any U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britton_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britton-42">[42]</a></sup> Much of the state south of <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a> lies at a lower elevation than northern Florida, and is fairly level. Much of the state is at or near sea level.</p>\n<p>However, some places such as <a href="/wiki/Clearwater,_Florida" title="Clearwater, Florida">Clearwater</a> have <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontories</a> that rise 50 to 100\xc2\xa0ft (15 to 30\xc2\xa0m) above the water. Much of Central and North Florida, typically 25\xc2\xa0mi (40\xc2\xa0km) or more away from the coastline, have rolling hills with elevations ranging from 100 to 250\xc2\xa0ft (30 to 76\xc2\xa0m). The highest point in peninsular Florida (east and south of the <a href="/wiki/Suwannee_River" title="Suwannee River">Suwannee River</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sugarloaf_Mountain_(Florida)" title="Sugarloaf Mountain (Florida)">Sugarloaf Mountain</a>, is a 312-foot (95\xc2\xa0m) peak in <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_Florida" title="Lake County, Florida">Lake County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugarloaf_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sugarloaf-43">[43]</a></sup> On average, Florida is the flattest state in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Florida" title="Climate of Florida">Climate of Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Florida#Climate" title="Geography of Florida">Geography of Florida \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Climate</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Florida_hurricanes" title="List of Florida hurricanes">List of Florida hurricanes</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._state_temperature_extremes" title="U.S. state temperature extremes">U.S. state temperature extremes</a></div>\n<p>The climate of Florida is tempered somewhat by the fact that no part of the state is distant from the ocean. North of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Okeechobee" title="Lake Okeechobee">Lake Okeechobee</a>, the prevalent climate is <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen</a>: <i>Cfa</i>), while areas south of the lake (including the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>) have a true <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> (K\xc3\xb6ppen: <i>Aw</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ritter_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ritter-45">[45]</a></sup> Mean high temperatures for late July are primarily in the low 90s Fahrenheit (32\xe2\x80\x9334\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). Mean low temperatures for early to mid January range from the low 40s Fahrenheit (4\xe2\x80\x937\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) in north Florida to above 60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) from Miami on southward. With an average daily temperature of 70.7\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (21.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), it is the warmest state in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the summer, high temperatures in the state seldom exceed 100\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (38\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). Several record cold maxima have been in the 30s \xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x921 to 4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and record lows have been in the 10s (\xe2\x88\x9212 to \xe2\x88\x927\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). These temperatures normally extend at most a few days at a time in the northern and central parts of Florida. Southern Florida, however, rarely encounters freezing temperatures.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>The hottest temperature ever recorded in Florida was 109\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (43\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), which was set on June 29, 1931 in <a href="/wiki/Monticello,_Florida" title="Monticello, Florida">Monticello</a>. The coldest temperature was \xe2\x88\x922\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9219\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), on February 13, 1899, just 25 miles (40\xc2\xa0km) away, in Tallahassee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Due to its subtropical and tropical climate, Florida rarely receives measurable <a href="/wiki/Snow_in_Florida" title="Snow in Florida">snowfall</a>. However, on rare occasions, a combination of cold moisture and freezing temperatures can result in snowfall in the farthest northern regions. Frost, which is more common than snow, sometimes occurs in the panhandle.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">USDA</a> Plant <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zones</a> for the state range from zone 8a (no colder than 10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F or \xe2\x88\x9212\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) in the inland western <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_panhandle" title="Florida panhandle">panhandle</a> to zone 11b (no colder than 45\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F or 7\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) in the lower <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="13" style="text-align:center;font-size:120%;background:#E8EAFA;">Average high and low temperatures for various Florida cities</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#e5afaa; color:#000">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tallahassee,_Florida" title="Tallahassee, Florida">Tallahassee</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tlhweather_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-tlhweather-54">[54]</a></sup></td>\n<td>64/39</td>\n<td>68/42</td>\n<td>74/47</td>\n<td>80/52</td>\n<td>87/62</td>\n<td>91/70</td>\n<td>92/72</td>\n<td>92/72</td>\n<td>89/68</td>\n<td>82/57</td>\n<td>73/48</td>\n<td>66/41</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#c5dfe1; color:#000">\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tampa" title="Tampa">Tampa</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tpaweather_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-tpaweather-55">[55]</a></sup></td>\n<td>70/51</td>\n<td>73/54</td>\n<td>77/58</td>\n<td>81/62</td>\n<td>88/69</td>\n<td>90/74</td>\n<td>90/75</td>\n<td>91/76</td>\n<td>89/74</td>\n<td>85/67</td>\n<td>78/60</td>\n<td>72/54</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</center>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n<tr style="background:#e5afaa; color:#000">\n<td><b>\xc2\xb0C</b></td>\n<td><b>Jan</b></td>\n<td><b>Feb</b></td>\n<td><b>Mar</b></td>\n<td><b>Apr</b></td>\n<td><b>May</b></td>\n<td><b>Jun</b></td>\n<td><b>Jul</b></td>\n<td><b>Aug</b></td>\n<td><b>Sep</b></td>\n<td><b>Oct</b></td>\n<td><b>Nov</b></td>\n<td><b>Dec</b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#f8f3ca; color:#000">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a></td>\n<td>18/6</td>\n<td>20/7</td>\n<td>23/10</td>\n<td>26/13</td>\n<td>30/17</td>\n<td>32/21</td>\n<td>33/23</td>\n<td>33/23</td>\n<td>31/21</td>\n<td>27/16</td>\n<td>23/11</td>\n<td>19/7</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#c5dfe1; color:#000">\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami</a></td>\n<td>24/16</td>\n<td>26/17</td>\n<td>27/18</td>\n<td>28/20</td>\n<td>31/23</td>\n<td>32/24</td>\n<td>33/25</td>\n<td>33/25</td>\n<td>32/24</td>\n<td>30/23</td>\n<td>28/20</td>\n<td>26/17</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#f8f3ca; color:#000">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a></td>\n<td>22/9</td>\n<td>23/11</td>\n<td>26/13</td>\n<td>28/16</td>\n<td>31/19</td>\n<td>33/22</td>\n<td>33/23</td>\n<td>33/23</td>\n<td>32/23</td>\n<td>29/19</td>\n<td>26/15</td>\n<td>23/11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#c5dfe1; color:#000">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">Pensacola</a></td>\n<td>16/6</td>\n<td>18/8</td>\n<td>21/11</td>\n<td>24/14</td>\n<td>29/19</td>\n<td>32/22</td>\n<td>32/23</td>\n<td>32/23</td>\n<td>31/21</td>\n<td>27/16</td>\n<td>21/10</td>\n<td>17/7</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#f8f3ca; color:#000">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tallahassee,_Florida" title="Tallahassee, Florida">Tallahassee</a></td>\n<td>18/4</td>\n<td>20/6</td>\n<td>23/8</td>\n<td>27/11</td>\n<td>31/17</td>\n<td>33/21</td>\n<td>33/22</td>\n<td>33/22</td>\n<td>32/20</td>\n<td>28/14</td>\n<td>23/9</td>\n<td>19/5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="background:#c5dfe1; color:#000">\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tampa" title="Tampa">Tampa</a></td>\n<td>21/11</td>\n<td>23/12</td>\n<td>25/14</td>\n<td>27/17</td>\n<td>31/21</td>\n<td>32/23</td>\n<td>32/24</td>\n<td>33/24</td>\n<td>32/23</td>\n<td>29/19</td>\n<td>26/16</td>\n<td>22/12</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</center>\n<p>Florida\'s nickname is the "Sunshine State", but severe weather is a common occurrence in the state. Central Florida is known as the lightning capital of the United States, as it experiences more lightning strikes than anywhere else in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lightning_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-lightning-56">[56]</a></sup> Florida has one of the highest average precipitation levels of any state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> in large part because afternoon thunderstorms are common in much of the state from late spring until early autumn. A narrow eastern part of the state including Orlando and Jacksonville receives between 2,400 and 2,800 hours of sunshine annually. The rest of the state, including Miami, receives between 2,800 and 3,200 hours annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Florida leads the United States in tornadoes per area (when including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterspouts" title="Waterspouts">waterspouts</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterspout_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-waterspout-59">[59]</a></sup> but they do not typically reach the intensity of those in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midwest" title="Midwest">Midwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. Hail often accompanies the most severe thunderstorms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">Hurricanes</a> pose a severe threat each year during the June 1 to November 30 hurricane season, particularly from August to October. Florida is the most hurricane-prone state, with subtropical or tropical water on a lengthy coastline. Of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_4" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">category 4</a> or higher storms that have struck the United States, 83% have either hit Florida or Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fltoday_fact_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-fltoday_fact-60">[60]</a></sup> From 1851 to 2006, Florida was struck by 114 hurricanes, 37 of them major\xe2\x80\x94<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_3" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">category 3</a> and above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fltoday_fact_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-fltoday_fact-60">[60]</a></sup> It is rare for a hurricane season to pass without any impact in the state by at least a tropical storm.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>In 1992, Florida was the site of what was then the costliest weather disaster in U.S. history, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a>, which caused more than $25 billion in damage when it struck during August; it held that distinction until 2005, when Hurricane Katrina surpassed it. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a>\xe2\x80\x94the second-most expensive hurricane in Florida history\xe2\x80\x94landed just south of <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island</a> in October 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft091231_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-ft091231-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watchdog_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Watchdog-62">[62]</a></sup> Although tropical storms would affect the state, it would be eleven years until the next hurricane (<a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hermine" title="Hurricane Hermine">Hurricane Hermine</a>) struck the state, and twelve years until the next major hurricane. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> struck the state where Wilma did in 2017.</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140.66666666667px">\n<div style="width: Florida, but has occurred in every major Florida city at least once.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" Miami\'s tropical climate makes it a top tourist destination in the winter.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Florida" title="List of mammals of Florida">List of mammals of Florida</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snakes_of_Florida" title="Snakes of Florida">Snakes of Florida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_invasive_marine_fish_in_Florida" title="List of invasive marine fish in Florida">List of invasive marine fish in Florida</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anhingatrailalligator.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="725" data-file-width="1019" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anhingatrailalligator.png/250px-Anhingatrailalligator.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anhingatrailalligator.png/375px-Anhingatrailalligator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Anhingatrailalligator.png/500px-Anhingatrailalligator.png 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anhingatrailalligator.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn <a href="/wiki/American_alligator" title="American alligator">alligator</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Everglades" title="Florida Everglades">Florida Everglades</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Florida is host to many types of wildlife including:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Marine mammals: <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short-finned_pilot_whale" title="Short-finned pilot whale">short-finned pilot whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_manatee" title="West Indian manatee">West Indian manatee</a></li>\n<li>Mammals: <a href="/wiki/Florida_panther" title="Florida panther">Florida panther</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_river_otter" title="Northern river otter">northern river otter</a>, mink, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_cottontail_rabbit" title="Eastern cottontail rabbit">eastern cottontail rabbit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marsh_rabbit" title="Marsh rabbit">marsh rabbit</a>, raccoon, striped skunk, squirrel, <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">white-tailed deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Key_deer" title="Key deer">Key deer</a>, bobcats, <a href="/wiki/Gray_fox" title="Gray fox">gray fox</a>, coyote, wild boar, <a href="/wiki/Florida_black_bear" title="Florida black bear">Florida black bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nine-banded_armadillo" title="Nine-banded armadillo">nine-banded armadillos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_opossum" title="Virginia opossum">Virginia opossum</a></li>\n<li>Reptiles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crotalus_adamanteus" title="Crotalus adamanteus">eastern diamondback</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sistrurus_miliarius_barbouri" title="Sistrurus miliarius barbouri">pygmy rattlesnakes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gopherus_polyphemus" title="Gopherus polyphemus">gopher tortoise</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_turtle" title="Green turtle">green</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherback sea turtles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drymarchon" title="Drymarchon">eastern indigo snake</a>. In 2012, there were about one million <a href="/wiki/American_alligator" title="American alligator">American alligators</a> and 1,500 <a href="/wiki/American_crocodile" title="American crocodile">crocodiles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Birds: <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon">peregrine falcon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_caracara" title="Northern caracara">northern caracara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snail_kite" title="Snail kite">snail kite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osprey" title="Osprey">osprey</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_white_pelican" title="American white pelican">white</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_pelican" title="Brown pelican">brown pelicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larus" title="Larus">sea gulls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whooping_crane" title="Whooping crane">whooping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandhill_crane" title="Sandhill crane">sandhill cranes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roseate_spoonbill" title="Roseate spoonbill">roseate spoonbill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_scrub_jay" title="Florida scrub jay">Florida scrub jay</a> (state <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>), and others. One subspecies of wild turkey, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meleagris_gallopavo" title="Meleagris gallopavo">Meleagris gallopavo</a></i>, namely subspecies <i>osceola</i>, is found only in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The state is a wintering location for many species of eastern North American birds.\n<ul>\n<li>As a result of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, there have been small numbers of several new species normally native to cooler areas to the north: <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">snowy owls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snow_bunting" title="Snow bunting">snow buntings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_duck" title="Harlequin duck">harlequin ducks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Razorbill" title="Razorbill">razorbills</a>. These have been seen in the northern part of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft140107_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-ft140107-66">[66]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>Invertebrates: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpenter_ants" title="Carpenter ants">carpenter ants</a>, termites, <a href="/wiki/American_cockroach" title="American cockroach">American cockroach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africanized_bee" title="Africanized bee">Africanized bees</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_blue" title="Miami blue">Miami blue</a> butterfly, and the <a href="/wiki/Gonatista_grisea" title="Gonatista grisea">grizzled mantis</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The only known calving area for the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">northern right whale</a> is off the coasts of Florida and Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whale_habitat_could_grow_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whale_habitat_could_grow-67">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_black_bear" title="Florida black bear">native bear</a> population has risen from a historic low of 300 in the 1970s, to 3,000 in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Since their accidental importation from South America into North America in the 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Red_imported_fire_ant" title="Red imported fire ant">red imported fire ant</a> population has increased its territorial range to include most of the southern United States, including Florida. They are more aggressive than most native ant species and have a painful sting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Not_all_alien_invaders_are_from_outer_space_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Not_all_alien_invaders_are_from_outer_space-69">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A number of non-native snakes and lizards have been released in the wild. In 2010 the state created a hunting season for <a href="/wiki/Burmese_python" title="Burmese python">Burmese</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_python" title="Indian python">Indian pythons</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_rock_python" title="African rock python">African rock pythons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_anaconda" title="Green anaconda">green anacondas</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nile_monitor_lizard" title="Nile monitor lizard">Nile monitor lizards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_creates_season_for_hunting_pythons_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-State_creates_season_for_hunting_pythons-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Green_iguana" title="Green iguana">Green iguanas</a> have also established a firm population in the southern part of the state.</p>\n<p>There are about 500,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Razorback" title="Razorback">feral pigs</a> in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Key_deer_male.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Key_deer_male.jpg/360px-Key_deer_male.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Key_deer_male.jpg/480px-Key_deer_male.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Key_deer" title="Key deer">Key deer</a> in the lower <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 148.66666666667px">\n<div href="/wiki/Florida_scrub_jay" title="Florida scrub jay">Florida scrub jay</a> is found only in Florida.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185.33333333333px">\n<div 99.333333333333px">\n<div style="width: 99.333333333333px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 97.333333333333px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/Whooping_crane" title="Whooping crane">Whooping crane</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span></h3>\n<p>There are about 3,000 different types of <a href="/wiki/Wildflower" title="Wildflower">wildflowers</a> in Florida. This is the third-most diverse state in the union, behind California and Texas, both larger states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On the east coast of the state, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangroves" title="Mangroves">mangroves</a> have normally dominated the coast from <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_Beach,_Florida" title="Cocoa Beach, Florida">Cocoa Beach</a> southward; <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">salt marshes</a> from <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> northward. From St. Augustine south to Cocoa Beach, the coast fluctuates between the two, depending on the annual weather conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft140107_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-ft140107-66">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">\n<div style="width: 182px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg/270px-Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg/405px-Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg/540px-Everglades_National_Park_cypress.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Everglades_National_Park" title="Everglades National Park">Everglades National Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Florida" title="Southern Florida">Southern Florida</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n<div style="margin:0px Honda Key">Bahia Honda</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ocala_National_Forest" title="Ocala National Forest">Ocala National Forest</a> in Central and Northern Florida.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_talbot_islands_state_park_2.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="773" height="120"
