class="gallerytext">\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timucuan_Ecological_and_Historic_Preserve" title="Timucuan Ecological and Historic Preserve">Timucuan Ecological and Historic Preserve</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_Florida" title="Northeast Florida">Northeast Florida</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2128" data-file-width="2800" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg/250px-Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg/375px-Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg/500px-Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crandon_Park_Modified.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe beaches of <a href="/wiki/Key_Biscayne,_Florida" title="Key Biscayne, Florida">Key Biscayne</a> in Miami.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Florida" title="Environment of Florida">Environment of Florida</a></div>\n<p>Florida is a low per capita energy user.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Consumption_by_Source_and_Total_Consumption_per_Capita.2C_Ranked_by_State.2C_2004_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Consumption_by_Source_and_Total_Consumption_per_Capita.2C_Ranked_by_State.2C_2004-73">[73]</a></sup> It is estimated that approximately 4% of energy in the state is generated through renewable resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoE-profile_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-DoE-profile-74">[74]</a></sup> Florida\'s energy production is 6% of the nation\'s total energy output, while total production of pollutants is lower, with figures of 6% for <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxide</a>, 5% for <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, and 4% for <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoE-profile_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-DoE-profile-74">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<p>All potable water resources have been controlled by the state government through five regional water authorities since 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Red_tide" title="Red tide">Red tide</a> has been an issue on the southwest coast of Florida, as well as other areas. While there has been a great deal of conjecture over the cause of the toxic algae bloom, there is no evidence that it is being caused by pollution or that there has been an increase in the duration or frequency of red tides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tide.27s_toxins_trouble_lungs_ashore_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tide.27s_toxins_trouble_lungs_ashore-76">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_panther" title="Florida panther">Florida panther</a> is close to extinction. A record 23 were killed in 2009 predominately by automobile collisions, leaving about 100 individuals in the wild. The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biological_Diversity" title="Center for Biological Diversity">Center for Biological Diversity</a> and others have therefore called for a special <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected area</a> for the panther to be established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_number_of_panthers_killed_by_vehicles_in_2009_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Record_number_of_panthers_killed_by_vehicles_in_2009-77">[77]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manatees" title="Manatees">Manatees</a> are also dying at a rate higher than their reproduction.</p>\n<p>Much of Florida has an elevation of less than 12 feet (3.7\xc2\xa0m), including many populated areas. Therefore, it is susceptible to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" title="Current sea level rise">rising sea levels</a> associated with <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS62013_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS62013-78">[78]</a></sup> The Atlantic beaches that are vital to the state\'s economy are being washed out to sea due to rising sea levels caused by climate change. The Miami beach area, close to the continental shelf, is running out of accessible offshore sand reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Florida" title="Geology of Florida">Geology of Florida</a></div>\n<p>The Florida peninsula is a porous <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> of <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> sitting atop <a href="/wiki/Bedrock" title="Bedrock">bedrock</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Platform" title="Florida Platform">Florida Platform</a>. The largest deposits of <a href="/wiki/Potash" title="Potash">potash</a> in the United States are found in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Industry_overview_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Industry_overview-80">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Extended systems of underwater caves, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinkholes" title="Sinkholes">sinkholes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrosphere)" title="Spring (hydrosphere)">springs</a> are found throughout the state and supply most of the water used by residents. The limestone is topped with <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sandy</a> soils deposited as ancient beaches over millions of years as global sea levels rose and fell. During the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, lower sea levels and a drier climate revealed a much wider peninsula, largely <a href="/wiki/Temperate_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Temperate grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">savanna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida.27s_Geological_History_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Florida.27s_Geological_History-81">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">Everglades</a>, an enormously wide, slow-flowing river encompasses the southern tip of the peninsula. Sinkhole damage claims on property in the state exceeded a total of $2 billion from 2006 through 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Florida is tied for last place as having the fewest earthquakes of any U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-More_earthquakes_than_usual.3F_Not_really._84-0"><a href="#cite_note-More_earthquakes_than_usual.3F_Not_really.-84">[84]</a></sup> Earthquakes are rare because Florida is not located near any <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic plate</a> boundaries.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Florida" title="Demographics of Florida">Demographics of Florida</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Florida" title="Culture of Florida">Culture of Florida</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florida_population_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Florida_population_map.png/220px-Florida_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Florida_population_map.png/330px-Florida_population_map.png 1.5x, text-align: center;">17.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center"><b>Est. 2016</b></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px;">20,612,439</td>\n<td style="font-size:85%"></td>\n<td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">9.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:left">\n<center>Sources: 1910\xe2\x80\x932010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><br/>\n2016 Estimate<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-86">[86]</a></sup></center>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Florida was 20,271,272 on July 1, 2015, a 7.82% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-86">[86]</a></sup> The population of Florida in the 2010 census was 18,801,310.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Florida was the seventh fastest-growing state in the U.S. in the 12-month period ending July 1, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Florida was located between <a href="/wiki/Fort_Meade,_Florida" title="Fort Meade, Florida">Fort Meade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frostproof,_Florida" title="Frostproof, Florida">Frostproof</a>. The center of population has moved less than 5 miles (8\xc2\xa0km) to the east and approximately 1 mile (1.6\xc2\xa0km) to the north between 1980 and 2010 and has been located in <a href="/wiki/Polk_County,_Florida" title="Polk County, Florida">Polk County</a> since the <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_Census" title="1960 United States Census">1960 census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The population exceeded 19.7 million by December 2014, surpassing the population of the state of <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Florida contains the highest percentage of people over 65 (17%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> There were 186,102 military retirees living in the state in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Retired_Military_Personnel_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Retired_Military_Personnel-92">[92]</a></sup> About two-thirds of the population was born in another state, the second highest in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">illegal immigrants</a> constituted an estimated 5.7% of the population. This was the sixth highest percentage of any U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Arizona_law_puts_police_in_.27tenuous.27_spot_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Arizona_law_puts_police_in_.27tenuous.27_spot-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> There were an estimated 675,000 illegal immigrants in the state in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A 2013 Gallup poll indicated that 47% of the residents agreed that Florida was the best state to live in. Results in other states ranged from a low of 18% to a high of 77%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">Settlements</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_urbanized_areas_in_Florida_(by_population)" title="List of urbanized areas in Florida (by population)">List of urbanized areas in Florida (by population)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_statistical_areas" title="Florida statistical areas">Florida statistical areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Florida" title="List of municipalities in Florida">List of municipalities in Florida</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Florida locations by per capita income">Florida locations by per capita income</a></div>\n<p>The legal name in Florida for a city, town or village is "municipality". In Florida there is no legal difference between towns, villages and cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2012, 75% of the population lived within 10 miles (16\xc2\xa0km) of the coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="841" data-file-width="865" height="321" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Florida_counties_map.png/330px-Florida_counties_map.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Florida_counties_map.png/660px-Florida_counties_map.png 2x" width="330"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florida_counties_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA map of Florida showing the 67 county names and boundaries.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> in the state as well as the entire southeastern United States is the <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami metropolitan area</a>, with about 6.06 million people. The <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Area" title="Tampa Bay Area">Tampa Bay Area</a>, with over 3.02 million people, is the second largest; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando_metropolitan_area" title="Orlando metropolitan area">Orlando metropolitan area</a>, with over 2.44 million people, is the third; and the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_metropolitan_area" title="Jacksonville metropolitan area">Jacksonville metropolitan area</a>, with over 1.47 million people, is fourth.</p>\n<p>Florida has 22 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">Metropolitan Statistical Areas</a> (MSAs) defined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">United States Office of Management and Budget</a> (OMB). 43 of Florida\'s 67 counties are in a MSA.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="601" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png/220px-Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png/330px-Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png/440px-Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ancestry-Florida-by_county-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPredominant ancestry in Florida in 2010</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<table href="#cite_note-census-101">[101]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></th>\n<th>2013</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White (includes White Hispanics)</a></td>\n<td>84.2%</td>\n<td>83.1%</td>\n<td>78.0%</td>\n<td>75.0%</td>\n<td>78.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a></td>\n<td>15.3%</td>\n<td>13.6%</td>\n<td>14.6%</td>\n<td>16.0%</td>\n<td>16.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a></td>\n<td>0.2%</td>\n<td>1.2%</td>\n<td>1.7%</td>\n<td>2.4%</td>\n<td>2.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native</a></td>\n<td>0.1%</td>\n<td>0.3%</td>\n<td>0.3%</td>\n<td>0.4%</td>\n<td>0.5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">Other race</a></td>\n<td>0.1%</td>\n<td>1.8%</td>\n<td>3.0%</td>\n<td>3.6%</td>\n<td>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a></td>\n<td>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>2.3%</td>\n<td>2.5%</td>\n<td>1.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">Non-Hispanic whites</a></td>\n<td>77.9%</td>\n<td>73.2%</td>\n<td>65.4%</td>\n<td>57.9%</td>\n<td>56.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_or_Latino_American" title="Hispanic or Latino American">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race)</td>\n<td>6.6%</td>\n<td>12.2%</td>\n<td>16.8%</td>\n<td>22.5%</td>\n<td>23.6%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino" title="Hispanic and Latino">Hispanic and Latinos</a> of any race made up 22.5% of the population in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> As of 2011, 57% of Florida\'s population younger than age 1 were minorities (meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2010, 6.9% of the population (1,269,765) considered themselves to be of only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_people" title="American people">American</a> ancestry (regardless of race or ethnicity).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLdemo_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLdemo-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLpop_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLpop-107">[107]</a></sup> Many of these were of English or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">Scotch-Irish</a> descent; however, their families have lived in the state for so long, that they choose to identify as having "American" ancestry or do not know their ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Factstreet_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Factstreet-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In the 1980 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_census" title="United States census">United States census</a> the largest ancestry group reported in Florida was English with 2,232,514 Floridians claiming that they were of English or mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English American</a> ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Some of their ancestry went back to the original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thirteen_colonies" title="Thirteen colonies">thirteen colonies</a>.</p>\n<p>As of 2010, those of (non-Hispanic white) European ancestry accounted for 57.9% of Florida\'s population. Out of the 57.9%, the largest groups were 12.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_people" title="German people">German</a> (2,212,391), 10.7% <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> (1,979,058), 8.8% <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> (1,629,832), 6.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> (1,215,242), 2.8% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">Polish</a> (511,229), and 2.7% <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> (504,641).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLdemo_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-FLdemo-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLpop_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-FLpop-107">[107]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White Americans</a> of all European backgrounds are present in all areas of the state. In 1970, non-Hispanic whites were nearly 80% of Florida\'s population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> ancestry are present in large numbers in all the urban/suburban areas across the state. Some native white Floridians, especially those who have descended from long-time Florida families, may refer to themselves as "<a href="/wiki/Florida_cracker" title="Florida cracker">Florida crackers</a>"; others see the term as a derogatory one. Like whites in most of the other Southern states, they descend mainly from English and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">Scots-Irish</a> settlers, as well as some other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_American" title="British American">British American</a> settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami,_Florida.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="600" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg/250px-Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg/375px-Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg/500px-Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami%2C_Florida.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_American_men_playing_dominoes_in_Little_Havana_Miami,_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">Cuban</a> men playing dominoes in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Little_Havana" title="Little Havana">Little Havana</a>. In 2010, Cubans made up 34.4% of Miami\'s population and 6.5% of Florida\'s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HisLatFlo_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-HisLatFlo-118">[118]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>As of 2010, those of Hispanic or Latino ancestry accounted for 22.5% (4,223,806) of Florida\'s population. Out of the 22.5%, the largest groups were 6.5% (1,213,438) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_people" title="Cuban people">Cuban</a>, 4.5% (847,550) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Rican</a>, 3.3% (629,718) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">Mexican</a>, and 1.6% (300,414) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_people" title="Colombian people">Colombian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HisLatFlo_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-HisLatFlo-118">[118]</a></sup> Florida\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" title="Hispanics in the United States">Hispanic</a> population includes large communities of <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Americans" title="Cuban Americans">Cuban Americans</a> in Miami and Tampa, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">Puerto Ricans</a> in Orlando and Tampa, and Mexican/Central American migrant workers. The Hispanic community continues to grow more affluent and mobile. As of 2011, 57.0% of Florida\'s children under the age of 1 belonged to minority groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Florida has a large and diverse Hispanic population, with Cubans and Puerto Ricans being the largest groups in the state. Nearly 80% of Cuban Americans live in Florida, especially South Florida where there is a long-standing and affluent Cuban community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Florida has the second largest Puerto Rican population after New York, as well as the fastest-growing in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Puerto Ricans are more widespread throughout the state, though the heaviest concentrations are in the Orlando area of Central Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As of 2010, those of African ancestry accounted for 16.0% of Florida\'s population, which includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African Americans</a>. Out of the 16.0%, 4.0% (741,879) were <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean_American" title="Afro-Caribbean American">Afro-Caribbean American</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLdemo_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-FLdemo-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLpop_107-2"><a href="#cite_note-FLpop-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HisLatFlo_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-HisLatFlo-118">[118]</a></sup> During the early 1900s, <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black people</a> made up nearly half of the state\'s population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1870census_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-1870census-123">[123]</a></sup> In response to segregation, disfranchisement and agricultural depression, many African Americans migrated from Florida to northern cities in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>, in waves from 1910 to 1940, and again starting in the later 1940s. They moved for jobs, better education for their children and the chance to vote and participate in society. By 1960 the proportion of African Americans in the state had declined to 18%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Census_Browser:_1960_US_Census_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Census_Browser:_1960_US_Census-124">[124]</a></sup> Conversely large numbers of northern <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">whites</a> moved to the state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today, large concentrations of black residents can be found in northern and central Florida. Aside from blacks descended from African slaves brought to the US south, there are also large numbers of blacks of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" title="West Indian American">West Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="African immigration to the United States">recent African</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Black_Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Black Hispanic and Latino Americans">Afro-Latino</a> immigrant origins, especially in the Miami/South Florida area.</p>\n<p>In 2016, Florida had the highest percentage of West Indians in the United States at 4.5%, with 2.3% (483,874) from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_people" title="Haitian people">Haitian</a> ancestry, 1.5% (303,527) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" title="Jamaican people">Jamaican</a>, and 0.2% (31,966) <a href="/wiki/Bahamians" title="Bahamians">Bahamian</a>, with the other West Indian groups making up the rest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As of 2010, those of Asian ancestry accounted for 2.4% of Florida\'s population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLdemo_106-3"><a href="#cite_note-FLdemo-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLpop_107-3"><a href="#cite_note-FLpop-107">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pardon_our_dust.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Pardon_our_dust.jpg/200px-Pardon_our_dust.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Pardon_our_dust.jpg/300px-Pardon_our_dust.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Pardon_our_dust.jpg/400px-Pardon_our_dust.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pardon_our_dust.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n20% of Floridians speak Spanish, the second-most widely-spoken language.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Florida#Languages" title="Demographics of Florida">Demographics of Florida \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Languages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Miami_accent" title="Miami accent">Miami accent</a></div>\n<p>In 1988 English was affirmed as the state\'s <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Constitution" title="Florida Constitution">Florida Constitution</a>. Spanish is also widely spoken, especially as immigration has continued from Latin America. Twenty percent of the population speak Spanish as their first language. Twenty-seven percent of Florida\'s population reports speaking a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English, and more than 200 first languages other than English are spoken at home in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacDonald_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonald-127">[127]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The most common languages spoken in Florida as a first language in 2010 are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-MLA-126">[126]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>73%\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 English</li>\n<li>20%\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 Spanish</li>\n<li>2%\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 Haitian Creole</li>\n<li>Other languages comprise less than 1% spoken by the state\'s population</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="857" data-file-width="1142" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg/250px-Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg/375px-Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg/500px-Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami_Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary" title="Miami Cathedral of Saint Mary">Miami Cathedral of Saint Mary</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> is the largest single religious denomination in the state.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <i>2014 Pew Religious Landscape Survey</i> showed the religious makeup of the state was as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Christian 70%\n<ul>\n<li>24% <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a></li>\n<li>21% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a></li>\n<li>14% <a href="/wiki/Mainline_Protestant" title="Mainline Protestant">Mainline Protestant</a></li>\n<li>8% <a href="/wiki/Black_church" title="Black church">Black Protestant</a></li>\n<li>3% Other Christian</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>3% Jewish</li>\n<li>3% Other non-Christian faiths</li>\n<li>24% Unaffiliated</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In 2010, the three largest denominational groups in Florida were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-129">[129]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Florida is mostly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> is the single largest denomination in the state, due in significant part to the state\'s large Hispanic population. There is also a sizable <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">Jewish</a> community, located mainly in <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a>; this is the largest Jewish population in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">South</a> and the third-largest in the U.S. behind those of New York and California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Florida" title="Government of Florida">Government of Florida</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Florida_Governors" title="List of Florida Governors">List of Florida Governors</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Congressional_Delegations_from_Florida" title="United States Congressional Delegations from Florida">United States Congressional Delegations from Florida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida_Cabinet" title="Florida Cabinet">Florida Cabinet</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg/190px-Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg/285px-Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg/380px-Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Florida_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Capitol" title="Florida State Capitol">Florida Capitol</a> buildings</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The basic structure, duties, function, and operations of the government of the state of Florida are defined and established by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Constitution" title="Florida Constitution">Florida Constitution</a>, which establishes the basic law of the state and guarantees various rights and freedoms of the people. The state government consists of three separate branches: judicial, executive, and legislative. The legislature enacts bills, which, if signed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Florida" title="Governor of Florida">governor</a>, become <a href="/wiki/Florida_Statutes" title="Florida Statutes">law</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Legislature" title="Florida Legislature">Florida Legislature</a> comprises the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Senate" title="Florida Senate">Florida Senate</a>, which has 40 members, and the <a href="/wiki/Florida_House_of_Representatives" title="Florida House of Representatives">Florida House of Representatives</a>, which has 120 members. The current Governor of Florida is <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Supreme_Court" title="Florida Supreme Court">Florida Supreme Court</a> consists of a Chief Justice and six Justices.</p>\n<p>Florida has 67 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Some reference materials may show only 66 because <a href="/wiki/Duval_County,_Florida" title="Duval County, Florida">Duval County</a> is consolidated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_of_Jacksonville" title="City of Jacksonville">City of Jacksonville</a>. There are 379 cities in Florida (out of 411) that report regularly to the Florida Department of Revenue, but there are other incorporated municipalities that do not. The state government\'s primary source of revenue is sales tax. Florida does not impose a personal <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>. The primary revenue source for cities and counties is property tax; unpaid taxes are subject to <a href="/wiki/Tax_sale" title="Tax sale">tax sales</a> which are held (at the county level) in May and (due to the extensive use of online bidding sites) are highly popular.</p>\n<p>There were 800 <a href="/wiki/Federal_Corrupt_Practices_Act" title="Federal Corrupt Practices Act">federal corruption</a> convictions from 1988 to 2007, more than any other state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections_history">Elections history</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Florida" title="Politics of Florida">Politics of Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Florida" title="Elections in Florida">Elections in Florida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Florida" title="Political party strength in Florida">Political party strength in Florida</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="6">Florida registered voters as of December 31, 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Party</th>\n<th>Number of Voters</th>\n<th>Percentage</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#3333FF;" width="10px"></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Florida_Democratic_Party" title="Florida Democratic Party">Democratic</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">4,905,705</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">37.85%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#E81B23;" width="10px"></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Florida" title="Republican Party of Florida">Republican</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">4,575,277</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">35.31%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#FDFD7F;" width="10px"></td>\n<td>Minor Parties</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">347,288</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2.68%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left" colspan="2" rowspan="1"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician#United_States" title="Independent politician">No Party Affiliation</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">3,130,915</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">24.16%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Total</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;"><b>12,959,185</b></th>\n<th style="text-align:center;">100%</th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>From 1952 to 1964, most voters were registered Democrats, but the state voted for the Republican presidential candidate in every election except for <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1964" title="United States presidential election, 1964">1964</a>. The following year, Congress passed and President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a>, providing for oversight of state practices and enforcement of constitutional voting rights for African Americans and other minorities in order to prevent the discrimination and disenfranchisement that had excluded most of them for decades from the political process.</p>\n<p>From the 1930s through much of the 1960s, Florida was essentially a one-party state dominated by white conservative Democrats, who together with other Democrats of the Solid South, exercised considerable control in Congress. They have gained slightly less federal money from national programs than they have paid in taxes <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>. Since the 1970s, conservative white voters in the state have largely shifted from the Democratic to the Republican Party. Though the majority of registered voters in Florida are Democrats <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>. It has continued to support Republican presidential candidates through the 20th century, except in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1976" title="United States presidential election, 1976">1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1996" title="United States presidential election, 1996">1996</a>, when the Democratic nominee was from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>.</p>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012</a> presidential elections, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> carried the state as a northern Democrat, attracting high voter turnout especially among the young, Independents, and minority voters, of whom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanics" title="Hispanics">Hispanics</a> comprise an increasingly large proportion. 2008 marked the first time since 1932, when <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> carried the state, that Florida was carried by a Northern Democrat for president.</p>\n<p>The first post-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">Reconstruction era</a> Republican elected to Congress from Florida was <a href="/wiki/William_C._Cramer" title="William C. Cramer">William C. Cramer</a> in 1954 from Pinellas County on the Gulf Coast,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_C._Cramer.2C_81.2C_a_Leader_Of_G.O.P._Resurgence_in_South_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-William_C._Cramer.2C_81.2C_a_Leader_Of_G.O.P._Resurgence_in_South-135">[135]</a></sup> where demographic changes were underway. In this period, African Americans were still <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">disenfranchised</a> by the state\'s constitution and discriminatory practices; in the 19th century they had made up most of the Republican Party. Cramer built a different Republican Party in Florida, attracting local white conservatives and transplants from northern and midwestern states. In 1966 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claude_R._Kirk,_Jr." title="Claude R. Kirk, Jr.">Claude R. Kirk, Jr.</a> was elected as the first post-Reconstruction Republican governor, in an upset election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Claude_Roy_Kirk.2C_Jr._136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Claude_Roy_Kirk.2C_Jr.-136">[136]</a></sup> In 1968 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_J._Gurney" title="Edward J. Gurney">Edward J. Gurney</a>, also a white conservative, was elected as the state\'s first post-reconstruction Republican US Senator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E._J._Gurney.2C_82.2C_Senator_Who_Backed_Nixon_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-E._J._Gurney.2C_82.2C_Senator_Who_Backed_Nixon-137">[137]</a></sup> In 1970 Democrats took the governorship and the open US Senate seat, and maintained dominance for years.</p>\n<p>Since the mid-20th century, Florida has been considered a <a href="/wiki/Bellwether" title="Bellwether">bellwether</a>, voting for 13 successful presidential candidates since 1952. It voted for the loser only three times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; font-size:95%; text-align:center; margin:10px">\n<caption><b>Presidential elections results</b></caption>\n<tr style="background:lightgrey;">\n<th>Year</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" style="background:#f0f0ff;">34.66% <i>1,448,816</i></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#fff3f3;"><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1980" title="United States presidential
